1	chapter
2	it was a bright cold day in april and the clocks were striking thirteen
3	winston smith his chin nuzzled into his breast in an effort to escape the vile wind slipped quickly through the glass doors of victory mansions though not quickly enough to prevent a swirl of gritty dust from entering along with him
4	the hallway smelt of boiled cabbage and old rag mats
5	at one end of it a coloured poster too large for indoor display had been tacked to the wall
6	it depicted simply an enormous face more than a metre wide the face of a man of about fortyfive with a heavy black moustache and ruggedly handsome features
7	winston made for the stairs
8	it was no use trying the lift
9	even at the best of times it was seldom working and at present the electric current was cut off during daylight hours
10	it was part of the economy drive in preparation for hate week
11	the flat was seven flights up and winston who was thirtynine and had a varicose ulcer above his right ankle went slowly resting several times on the way
12	on each landing opposite the liftshaft the poster with the enormous face gazed from the wall
13	it was one of those pictures which are so contrived that the eyes follow you about when you move
14	big brother is watching you the caption beneath it ran
15	inside the flat a fruity voice was reading out a list of figures which had something to do with the production of pigiron
16	the voice came from an oblong metal plaque like a dulled mirror which formed part of the surface of the righthand wall
17	winston turned a switch and the voice sank somewhat though the words were still distinguishable
18	the instrument the telescreen it was called could be dimmed but there was no way of shutting it off completely
19	he moved over to the window a smallish frail figure the meagreness of his body merely emphasized by the blue overalls which were the uniform of the party
20	his hair was very fair his face naturally sanguine his skin roughened by coarse soap and blunt razor blades and the cold of the winter that had just ended
21	outside even through the shut windowpane the world looked cold
22	down in the street little eddies of wind were whirling dust and torn paper into spirals and though the sun was shining and the sky a harsh blue there seemed to be no colour in anything except the posters that were plastered everywhere
23	the blackmoustachiod face gazed down from every commanding corner
24	there was one on the housefront immediately opposite
25	big brother is watching you the caption said while the dark eyes looked deep into winstons own
26	down at street level another poster torn at one corner flapped fitfully in the wind alternately covering and uncovering the single word ingsoc
27	in the far distance a helicopter skimmed down between the roofs hovered for an instant like a bluebottle and darted away again with a curving flight
28	it was the police patrol snooping into peoples windows
29	the patrols did not matter however
30	only the thought police mattered
31	behind winstons back the voice from the telescreen was still babbling away about pigiron and the overfulfilment of the ninth threeyear plan
32	the telescreen received and transmitted simultaneously
33	any sound that winston made above the level of a very low whisper would be picked up by it moreover so long as he remained within the field of vision which the metal plaque commanded he could be seen as well as heard
34	there was of course no way of knowing whether you were being watched at any given moment
35	how often or on what system the thought police plugged in on any individual wire was guesswork
36	it was even conceivable that they watched everybody all the time
37	but at any rate they could plug in your wire whenever they wanted to
38	you had to livedid live from habit that became instinctin the assumption that every sound you made was overheard and except in darkness every movement scrutinized
39	winston kept his back turned to the telescreen
40	it was safer though as he well knew even a back can be revealing
41	a kilometre away the ministry of truth his place of work towered vast and white above the grimy landscape
42	this he thought with a sort of vague distastethis was london chief city of airstrip one itself the third most populous of the provinces of oceania
43	he tried to squeeze out some childhood memory that should tell him whether london had always been quite like this
44	were there always these vistas of rotting nineteenthcentury houses their sides shored up with baulks of timber their windows patched with cardboard and their roofs with corrugated iron their crazy garden walls sagging in all directions
45	and the bombed sites where the plaster dust swirled in the air and the willowherb straggled over the heaps of rubble and the places where the bombs had cleared a larger patch and there had sprung up sordid colonies of wooden dwellings like chickenhouses
46	but it was no use he could not remember nothing remained of his childhood except a series of brightlit tableaux occurring against no background and mostly unintelligible
47	the ministry of truthminitrue in newspeak newspeak was the official language of oceania
48	for an account of its structure and etymology see appendix
49	was startlingly different from any other object in sight
50	it was an enormous pyramidal structure of glittering white concrete soaring up terrace after terrace metres into the air
51	from where winston stood it was just possible to read picked out on its white face in elegant lettering the three slogans of the party
52	war is peace
53	freedom is slavery
54	ignorance is strength
55	the ministry of truth contained it was said three thousand rooms above ground level and corresponding ramifications below
56	scattered about london there were just three other buildings of similar appearance and size
57	so completely did they dwarf the surrounding architecture that from the roof of victory mansions you could see all four of them simultaneously
58	they were the homes of the four ministries between which the entire apparatus of government was divided
59	the ministry of truth which concerned itself with news entertainment education and the fine arts
60	the ministry of peace which concerned itself with war
61	the ministry of love which maintained law and order
62	and the ministry of plenty which was responsible for economic affairs
63	their names in newspeak minitrue minipax miniluv and miniplenty
64	the ministry of love was the really frightening one
65	there were no windows in it at all
66	winston had never been inside the ministry of love nor within half a kilometre of it
67	it was a place impossible to enter except on official business and then only by penetrating through a maze of barbedwire entanglements steel doors and hidden machinegun nests
68	even the streets leading up to its outer barriers were roamed by gorillafaced guards in black uniforms armed with jointed truncheons
69	winston turned round abruptly
70	he had set his features into the expression of quiet optimism which it was advisable to wear when facing the telescreen
71	he crossed the room into the tiny kitchen
72	by leaving the ministry at this time of day he had sacrificed his lunch in the canteen and he was aware that there was no food in the kitchen except a hunk of darkcoloured bread which had got to be saved for tomorrows breakfast
73	he took down from the shelf a bottle of colourless liquid with a plain white label marked victory gin
74	it gave off a sickly oily smell as of chinese ricespirit
75	winston poured out nearly a teacupful nerved himself for a shock and gulped it down like a dose of medicine
76	instantly his face turned scarlet and the water ran out of his eyes
77	the stuff was like nitric acid and moreover in swallowing it one had the sensation of being hit on the back of the head with a rubber club
78	the next moment however the burning in his belly died down and the world began to look more cheerful
79	he took a cigarette from a crumpled packet marked victory cigarettes and incautiously held it upright whereupon the tobacco fell out on to the floor
80	with the next he was more successful
81	he went back to the livingroom and sat down at a small table that stood to the left of the telescreen
82	from the table drawer he took out a penholder a bottle of ink and a thick quartosized blank book with a red back and a marbled cover
83	for some reason the telescreen in the livingroom was in an unusual position
84	instead of being placed as was normal in the end wall where it could command the whole room it was in the longer wall opposite the window
85	to one side of it there was a shallow alcove in which winston was now sitting and which when the flats were built had probably been intended to hold bookshelves
86	by sitting in the alcove and keeping well back winston was able to remain outside the range of the telescreen so far as sight went
87	he could be heard of course but so long as he stayed in his present position he could not be seen
88	it was partly the unusual geography of the room that had suggested to him the thing that he was now about to do
89	but it had also been suggested by the book that he had just taken out of the drawer
90	it was a peculiarly beautiful book
91	its smooth creamy paper a little yellowed by age was of a kind that had not been manufactured for at least forty years past
92	he could guess however that the book was much older than that
93	he had seen it lying in the window of a frowsy little junkshop in a slummy quarter of the town just what quarter he did not now remember and had been stricken immediately by an overwhelming desire to possess it
94	party members were supposed not to go into ordinary shops dealing on the free market it was called but the rule was not strictly kept because there were various things such as shoelaces and razor blades which it was impossible to get hold of in any other way
95	he had given a quick glance up and down the street and then had slipped inside and bought the book for two dollars fifty
96	at the time he was not conscious of wanting it for any particular purpose
97	he had carried it guiltily home in his briefcase
98	even with nothing written in it it was a compromising possession
99	the thing that he was about to do was to open a diary
100	this was not illegal nothing was illegal since there were no longer any laws but if detected it was reasonably certain that it would be punished by death or at least by twentyfive years in a forcedlabour camp
101	winston fitted a nib into the penholder and sucked it to get the grease off
102	the pen was an archaic instrument seldom used even for signatures and he had procured one furtively and with some difficulty simply because of a feeling that the beautiful creamy paper deserved to be written on with a real nib instead of being scratched with an inkpencil
103	actually he was not used to writing by hand
104	apart from very short notes it was usual to dictate everything into the speakwrite which was of course impossible for his present purpose
105	he dipped the pen into the ink and then faltered for just a second
106	a tremor had gone through his bowels
107	to mark the paper was the decisive act
108	in small clumsy letters he wrote
109	april th
110	he sat back
111	a sense of complete helplessness had descended upon him
112	to begin with he did not know with any certainty that this was
113	it must be round about that date since he was fairly sure that his age was thirtynine and he believed that he had been born in or but it was never possible nowadays to pin down any date within a year or two
114	for whom it suddenly occurred to him to wonder was he writing this diary
115	for the future for the unborn
116	his mind hovered for a moment round the doubtful date on the page and then fetched up with a bump against the newspeak word doublethink
117	for the first time the magnitude of what he had undertaken came home to him
118	how could you communicate with the future
119	it was of its nature impossible
120	either the future would resemble the present in which case it would not listen to him or it would be different from it and his predicament would be meaningless
121	for some time he sat gazing stupidly at the paper
122	the telescreen had changed over to strident military music
123	it was curious that he seemed not merely to have lost the power of expressing himself but even to have forgotten what it was that he had originally intended to say
124	for weeks past he had been making ready for this moment and it had never crossed his mind that anything would be needed except courage
125	the actual writing would be easy
126	all he had to do was to transfer to paper the interminable restless monologue that had been running inside his head literally for years
127	at this moment however even the monologue had dried up
128	moreover his varicose ulcer had begun itching unbearably
129	he dared not scratch it because if he did so it always became inflamed
130	the seconds were ticking by
131	he was conscious of nothing except the blankness of the page in front of him the itching of the skin above his ankle the blaring of the music and a slight booziness caused by the gin
132	suddenly he began writing in sheer panic only imperfectly aware of what he was setting down
133	his small but childish handwriting straggled up and down the page shedding first its capital letters and finally even its full stops
134	april th
135	last night to the flicks
136	all war films
137	one very good one of a ship full of refugees being bombed somewhere in the mediterranean
138	audience much amused by shots of a great huge fat man trying to swim away with a helicopter after him first you saw him wallowing along in the water like a porpoise then you saw him through the helicopters gunsights then he was full of holes and the sea round him turned pink and he sank as suddenly as though the holes had let in the water audience shouting with laughter when he sank
139	then you saw a lifeboat full of children with a helicopter hovering over it
140	there was a middleaged woman might have been a jewess sitting up in the bow with a little boy about three years old in her arms
141	little boy screaming with fright and hiding his head between her breasts as if he was trying to burrow right into her and the woman putting her arms round him and comforting him although she was blue with fright herself all the time covering him up as much as possible as if she thought her arms could keep the bullets off him
142	then the helicopter planted a kilo bomb in among them terrific flash and the boat went all to matchwood
143	then there was a wonderful shot of a childs arm going up up up right up into the air a helicopter with a camera in its nose must have followed it up and there was a lot of applause from the party seats but a woman down in the prole part of the house suddenly started kicking up a fuss and shouting they didnt oughter of showed it not in front of kids they didnt it aint right not in front of kids it aint until the police turned her turned her out i dont suppose anything happened to her nobody cares what the proles say typical prole reaction they never
144	winston stopped writing partly because he was suffering from cramp
145	he did not know what had made him pour out this stream of rubbish
146	but the curious thing was that while he was doing so a totally different memory had clarified itself in his mind to the point where he almost felt equal to writing it down
147	it was he now realized because of this other incident that he had suddenly decided to come home and begin the diary today
148	it had happened that morning at the ministry if anything so nebulous could be said to happen
149	it was nearly eleven hundred and in the records department where winston worked they were dragging the chairs out of the cubicles and grouping them in the centre of the hall opposite the big telescreen in preparation for the two minutes hate
150	winston was just taking his place in one of the middle rows when two people whom he knew by sight but had never spoken to came unexpectedly into the room
151	one of them was a girl whom he often passed in the corridors
152	he did not know her name but he knew that she worked in the fiction department
153	presumablysince he had sometimes seen her with oily hands and carrying a spannershe had some mechanical job on one of the novelwriting machines
154	she was a boldlooking girl of about twentyseven with thick hair a freckled face and swift athletic movements
155	a narrow scarlet sash emblem of the junior antisex league was wound several times round the waist of her overalls just tightly enough to bring out the shapeliness of her hips
156	winston had disliked her from the very first moment of seeing her
157	he knew the reason
158	it was because of the atmosphere of hockeyfields and cold baths and community hikes and general cleanmindedness which she managed to carry about with her
159	he disliked nearly all women and especially the young and pretty ones
160	it was always the women and above all the young ones who were the most bigoted adherents of the party the swallowers of slogans the amateur spies and nosersout of unorthodoxy
161	but this particular girl gave him the impression of being more dangerous than most
162	once when they passed in the corridor she gave him a quick sidelong glance which seemed to pierce right into him and for a moment had filled him with black terror
163	the idea had even crossed his mind that she might be an agent of the thought police
164	that it was true was very unlikely
165	still he continued to feel a peculiar uneasiness which had fear mixed up in it as well as hostility whenever she was anywhere near him
166	the other person was a man named obrien a member of the inner party and holder of some post so important and remote that winston had only a dim idea of its nature
167	a momentary hush passed over the group of people round the chairs as they saw the black overalls of an inner party member approaching
168	obrien was a large burly man with a thick neck and a coarse humorous brutal face
169	in spite of his formidable appearance he had a certain charm of manner
170	he had a trick of resettling his spectacles on his nose which was curiously disarmingin some indefinable way curiously civilized
171	it was a gesture which if anyone had still thought in such terms might have recalled an eighteenthcentury nobleman offering his snuffbox
172	winston had seen obrien perhaps a dozen times in almost as many years
173	he felt deeply drawn to him and not solely because he was intrigued by the contrast between obriens urbane manner and his prizefighters physique
174	much more it was because of a secretly held beliefor perhaps not even a belief merely a hopethat obriens political orthodoxy was not perfect
175	something in his face suggested it irresistibly
176	and again perhaps it was not even unorthodoxy that was written in his face but simply intelligence
177	but at any rate he had the appearance of being a person that you could talk to if somehow you could cheat the telescreen and get him alone
178	winston had never made the smallest effort to verify this guess indeed there was no way of doing so
179	at this moment obrien glanced at his wristwatch saw that it was nearly eleven hundred and evidently decided to stay in the records department until the two minutes hate was over
180	he took a chair in the same row as winston a couple of places away
181	a small sandyhaired woman who worked in the next cubicle to winston was between them
182	the girl with dark hair was sitting immediately behind
183	the next moment a hideous grinding speech as of some monstrous machine running without oil burst from the big telescreen at the end of the room
184	it was a noise that set ones teeth on edge and bristled the hair at the back of ones neck
185	the hate had started
186	as usual the face of emmanuel goldstein the enemy of the people had flashed on to the screen
187	there were hisses here and there among the audience
188	the little sandyhaired woman gave a squeak of mingled fear and disgust
189	goldstein was the renegade and backslider who once long ago how long ago nobody quite remembered had been one of the leading figures of the party almost on a level with big brother himself and then had engaged in counterrevolutionary activities had been condemned to death and had mysteriously escaped and disappeared
190	the programmes of the two minutes hate varied from day to day but there was none in which goldstein was not the principal figure
191	he was the primal traitor the earliest defiler of the partys purity
192	all subsequent crimes against the party all treacheries acts of sabotage heresies deviations sprang directly out of his teaching
193	somewhere or other he was still alive and hatching his conspiracies perhaps somewhere beyond the sea under the protection of his foreign paymasters perhaps evenso it was occasionally rumouredin some hidingplace in oceania itself
194	winstons diaphragm was constricted
195	he could never see the face of goldstein without a painful mixture of emotions
196	it was a lean jewish face with a great fuzzy aureole of white hair and a small goatee bearda clever face and yet somehow inherently despicable with a kind of senile silliness in the long thin nose near the end of which a pair of spectacles was perched
197	it resembled the face of a sheep and the voice too had a sheeplike quality
198	goldstein was delivering his usual venomous attack upon the doctrines of the partyan attack so exaggerated and perverse that a child should have been able to see through it and yet just plausible enough to fill one with an alarmed feeling that other people less levelheaded than oneself might be taken in by it
199	he was abusing big brother he was denouncing the dictatorship of the party he was demanding the immediate conclusion of peace with eurasia he was advocating freedom of speech freedom of the press freedom of assembly freedom of thought he was crying hysterically that the revolution had been betrayedand all this in rapid polysyllabic speech which was a sort of parody of the habitual style of the orators of the party and even contained newspeak words more newspeak words indeed than any party member would normally use in real life
200	and all the while lest one should be in any doubt as to the reality which goldsteins specious claptrap covered behind his head on the telescreen there marched the endless columns of the eurasian armyrow after row of solidlooking men with expressionless asiatic faces who swam up to the surface of the screen and vanished to be replaced by others exactly similar
201	the dull rhythmic tramp of the soldiers boots formed the background to goldsteins bleating voice
202	before the hate had proceeded for thirty seconds uncontrollable exclamations of rage were breaking out from half the people in the room
203	the selfsatisfied sheeplike face on the screen and the terrifying power of the eurasian army behind it were too much to be borne besides the sight or even the thought of goldstein produced fear and anger automatically
204	he was an object of hatred more constant than either eurasia or eastasia since when oceania was at war with one of these powers it was generally at peace with the other
205	but what was strange was that although goldstein was hated and despised by everybody although every day and a thousand times a day on platforms on the telescreen in newspapers in books his theories were refuted smashed ridiculed held up to the general gaze for the pitiful rubbish that they werein spite of all this his influence never seemed to grow less
206	always there were fresh dupes waiting to be seduced by him
207	a day never passed when spies and saboteurs acting under his directions were not unmasked by the thought police
208	he was the commander of a vast shadowy army an underground network of conspirators dedicated to the overthrow of the state
209	the brotherhood its name was supposed to be
210	there were also whispered stories of a terrible book a compendium of all the heresies of which goldstein was the author and which circulated clandestinely here and there
211	it was a book without a title
212	people referred to it if at all simply as the book
213	but one knew of such things only through vague rumours
214	neither the brotherhood nor the book was a subject that any ordinary party member would mention if there was a way of avoiding it
215	in its second minute the hate rose to a frenzy
216	people were leaping up and down in their places and shouting at the tops of their voices in an effort to drown the maddening bleating voice that came from the screen
217	the little sandyhaired woman had turned bright pink and her mouth was opening and shutting like that of a landed fish
218	even obriens heavy face was flushed
219	he was sitting very straight in his chair his powerful chest swelling and quivering as though he were standing up to the assault of a wave
220	the darkhaired girl behind winston had begun crying out swine
221	swine
222	swine
223	and suddenly she picked up a heavy newspeak dictionary and flung it at the screen
224	it struck goldsteins nose and bounced off the voice continued inexorably
225	in a lucid moment winston found that he was shouting with the others and kicking his heel violently against the rung of his chair
226	the horrible thing about the two minutes hate was not that one was obliged to act a part but on the contrary that it was impossible to avoid joining in
227	within thirty seconds any pretence was always unnecessary
228	a hideous ecstasy of fear and vindictiveness a desire to kill to torture to smash faces in with a sledgehammer seemed to flow through the whole group of people like an electric current turning one even against ones will into a grimacing screaming lunatic
229	and yet the rage that one felt was an abstract undirected emotion which could be switched from one object to another like the flame of a blowlamp
230	thus at one moment winstons hatred was not turned against goldstein at all but on the contrary against big brother the party and the thought police and at such moments his heart went out to the lonely derided heretic on the screen sole guardian of truth and sanity in a world of lies
231	and yet the very next instant he was at one with the people about him and all that was said of goldstein seemed to him to be true
232	at those moments his secret loathing of big brother changed into adoration and big brother seemed to tower up an invincible fearless protector standing like a rock against the hordes of asia and goldstein in spite of his isolation his helplessness and the doubt that hung about his very existence seemed like some sinister enchanter capable by the mere power of his voice of wrecking the structure of civilization
233	it was even possible at moments to switch ones hatred this way or that by a voluntary act
234	suddenly by the sort of violent effort with which one wrenches ones head away from the pillow in a nightmare winston succeeded in transferring his hatred from the face on the screen to the darkhaired girl behind him
235	vivid beautiful hallucinations flashed through his mind
236	he would flog her to death with a rubber truncheon
237	he would tie her naked to a stake and shoot her full of arrows like saint sebastian
238	he would ravish her and cut her throat at the moment of climax
239	better than before moreover he realized why it was that he hated her
240	he hated her because she was young and pretty and sexless because he wanted to go to bed with her and would never do so because round her sweet supple waist which seemed to ask you to encircle it with your arm there was only the odious scarlet sash aggressive symbol of chastity
241	the hate rose to its climax
242	the voice of goldstein had become an actual sheeps bleat and for an instant the face changed into that of a sheep
243	then the sheepface melted into the figure of a eurasian soldier who seemed to be advancing huge and terrible his submachine gun roaring and seeming to spring out of the surface of the screen so that some of the people in the front row actually flinched backwards in their seats
244	but in the same moment drawing a deep sigh of relief from everybody the hostile figure melted into the face of big brother blackhaired blackmoustachiod full of power and mysterious calm and so vast that it almost filled up the screen
245	nobody heard what big brother was saying
246	it was merely a few words of encouragement the sort of words that are uttered in the din of battle not distinguishable individually but restoring confidence by the fact of being spoken
247	then the face of big brother faded away again and instead the three slogans of the party stood out in bold capitals
248	war is peace
249	freedom is slavery
250	ignorance is strength
251	but the face of big brother seemed to persist for several seconds on the screen as though the impact that it had made on everyones eyeballs was too vivid to wear off immediately
252	the little sandyhaired woman had flung herself forward over the back of the chair in front of her
253	with a tremulous murmur that sounded like my saviour
254	she extended her arms towards the screen
255	then she buried her face in her hands
256	it was apparent that she was uttering a prayer
257	at this moment the entire group of people broke into a deep slow rhythmical chant of bbbb
258	over and over again very slowly with a long pause between the first b and the seconda heavy murmurous sound somehow curiously savage in the background of which one seemed to hear the stamp of naked feet and the throbbing of tomtoms
259	for perhaps as much as thirty seconds they kept it up
260	it was a refrain that was often heard in moments of overwhelming emotion
261	partly it was a sort of hymn to the wisdom and majesty of big brother but still more it was an act of selfhypnosis a deliberate drowning of consciousness by means of rhythmic noise
262	winstons entrails seemed to grow cold
263	in the two minutes hate he could not help sharing in the general delirium but this subhuman chanting of bbbb
264	always filled him with horror
265	of course he chanted with the rest it was impossible to do otherwise
266	to dissemble your feelings to control your face to do what everyone else was doing was an instinctive reaction
267	but there was a space of a couple of seconds during which the expression of his eyes might conceivably have betrayed him
268	and it was exactly at this moment that the significant thing happenedif indeed it did happen
269	momentarily he caught obriens eye
270	obrien had stood up
271	he had taken off his spectacles and was in the act of resettling them on his nose with his characteristic gesture
272	but there was a fraction of a second when their eyes met and for as long as it took to happen winston knewyes he knewthat obrien was thinking the same thing as himself
273	an unmistakable message had passed
274	it was as though their two minds had opened and the thoughts were flowing from one into the other through their eyes
275	i am with you obrien seemed to be saying to him
276	i know precisely what you are feeling
277	i know all about your contempt your hatred your disgust
278	but dont worry i am on your side
279	and then the flash of intelligence was gone and obriens face was as inscrutable as everybody elses
280	that was all and he was already uncertain whether it had happened
281	such incidents never had any sequel
282	all that they did was to keep alive in him the belief or hope that others besides himself were the enemies of the party
283	perhaps the rumours of vast underground conspiracies were true after allperhaps the brotherhood really existed
284	it was impossible in spite of the endless arrests and confessions and executions to be sure that the brotherhood was not simply a myth
285	some days he believed in it some days not
286	there was no evidence only fleeting glimpses that might mean anything or nothing snatches of overheard conversation faint scribbles on lavatory wallsonce even when two strangers met a small movement of the hand which had looked as though it might be a signal of recognition
287	it was all guesswork very likely he had imagined everything
288	he had gone back to his cubicle without looking at obrien again
289	the idea of following up their momentary contact hardly crossed his mind
290	it would have been inconceivably dangerous even if he had known how to set about doing it
291	for a second two seconds they had exchanged an equivocal glance and that was the end of the story
292	but even that was a memorable event in the locked loneliness in which one had to live
293	winston roused himself and sat up straighter
294	he let out a belch
295	the gin was rising from his stomach
296	his eyes refocused on the page
297	he discovered that while he sat helplessly musing he had also been writing as though by automatic action
298	and it was no longer the same cramped awkward handwriting as before
299	his pen had slid voluptuously over the smooth paper printing in large neat capitals
300	down with big brother
301	down with big brother
302	down with big brother
303	down with big brother
304	down with big brother
305	over and over again filling half a page
306	he could not help feeling a twinge of panic
307	it was absurd since the writing of those particular words was not more dangerous than the initial act of opening the diary but for a moment he was tempted to tear out the spoiled pages and abandon the enterprise altogether
308	he did not do so however because he knew that it was useless
309	whether he wrote down with big brother or whether he refrained from writing it made no difference
310	whether he went on with the diary or whether he did not go on with it made no difference
311	the thought police would get him just the same
312	he had committedwould still have committed even if he had never set pen to paperthe essential crime that contained all others in itself
313	thoughtcrime they called it
314	thoughtcrime was not a thing that could be concealed for ever
315	you might dodge successfully for a while even for years but sooner or later they were bound to get you
316	it was always at nightthe arrests invariably happened at night
317	the sudden jerk out of sleep the rough hand shaking your shoulder the lights glaring in your eyes the ring of hard faces round the bed
318	in the vast majority of cases there was no trial no report of the arrest
319	people simply disappeared always during the night
320	your name was removed from the registers every record of everything you had ever done was wiped out your onetime existence was denied and then forgotten
321	you were abolished annihilated vaporized was the usual word

706	in the walls of the cubicle there were three orifices

708	this last was for the disposal of waste paper
709	similar slits existed in thousands or tens of thousands throughout the building not only in every room but at short intervals in every corridor
710	for some reason they were nicknamed memory holes
711	when one knew that any document was due for destruction or even when one saw a scrap of waste paper lying about it was an automatic action to lift the flap of the nearest memory hole and drop it in whereupon it would be whirled away on a current of warm air to the enormous furnaces which were hidden somewhere in the recesses of the building
712	winston examined the four slips of paper which he had unrolled
713	each contained a message of only one or two lines in the abbreviated jargonnot actually newspeak but consisting largely of newspeak wordswhich was used in the ministry for internal purposes
714	they ran
715	times bb speech malreported africa rectify
716	times forecasts yp th quarter misprints verify current issue
717	times miniplenty malquoted chocolate rectify
718	times reporting bb dayorder doubleplusungood refs unpersons rewrite fullwise upsub antefiling
719	with a faint feeling of satisfaction winston laid the fourth message aside
720	it was an intricate and responsible job and had better be dealt with last
721	the other three were routine matters though the second one would probably mean some tedious wading through lists of figures
722	winston dialled back numbers on the telescreen and called for the appropriate issues of the times which slid out of the pneumatic tube after only a few minutes delay
723	the messages he had received referred to articles or news items which for one reason or another it was thought necessary to alter or as the official phrase had it to rectify
724	for example it appeared from the times of the seventeenth of march that big brother in his speech of the previous day had predicted that the south indian front would remain quiet but that a eurasian offensive would shortly be launched in north africa
725	as it happened the eurasian higher command had launched its offensive in south india and left north africa alone
726	it was therefore necessary to rewrite a paragraph of big brothers speech in such a way as to make him predict the thing that had actually happened
727	or again the times of the nineteenth of december had published the official forecasts of the output of various classes of consumption goods in the fourth quarter of which was also the sixth quarter of the ninth threeyear plan
728	todays issue contained a statement of the actual output from which it appeared that the forecasts were in every instance grossly wrong
729	winstons job was to rectify the original figures by making them agree with the later ones
730	as for the third message it referred to a very simple error which could be set right in a couple of minutes
731	as short a time ago as february the ministry of plenty had issued a promise a categorical pledge were the official words that there would be no reduction of the chocolate ration during
732	actually as winston was aware the chocolate ration was to be reduced from thirty grammes to twenty at the end of the present week
733	all that was needed was to substitute for the original promise a warning that it would probably be necessary to reduce the ration at some time in april
734	as soon as winston had dealt with each of the messages he clipped his speakwritten corrections to the appropriate copy of the times and pushed them into the pneumatic tube
735	then with a movement which was as nearly as possible unconscious he crumpled up the original message and any notes that he himself had made and dropped them into the memory hole to be devoured by the flames
736	what happened in the unseen labyrinth to which the pneumatic tubes led he did not know in detail but he did know in general terms
737	as soon as all the corrections which happened to be necessary in any particular number of the times had been assembled and collated that number would be reprinted the original copy destroyed and the corrected copy placed on the files in its stead
738	this process of continuous alteration was applied not only to newspapers but to books periodicals pamphlets posters leaflets films soundtracks cartoons photographsto every kind of literature or documentation which might conceivably hold any political or ideological significance
739	day by day and almost minute by minute the past was brought up to date
740	in this way every prediction made by the party could be shown by documentary evidence to have been correct nor was any item of news or any expression of opinion which conflicted with the needs of the moment ever allowed to remain on record
741	all history was a palimpsest scraped clean and reinscribed exactly as often as was necessary
742	in no case would it have been possible once the deed was done to prove that any falsification had taken place
743	the largest section of the records department far larger than the one on which winston worked consisted simply of persons whose duty it was to track down and collect all copies of books newspapers and other documents which had been superseded and were due for destruction
744	a number of the times which might because of changes in political alignment or mistaken prophecies uttered by big brother have been rewritten a dozen times still stood on the files bearing its original date and no other copy existed to contradict it
745	books also were recalled and rewritten again and again and were invariably reissued without any admission that any alteration had been made
746	even the written instructions which winston received and which he invariably got rid of as soon as he had dealt with them never stated or implied that an act of forgery was to be committed always the reference was to slips errors misprints or misquotations which it was necessary to put right in the interests of accuracy
747	but actually he thought as he readjusted the ministry of plentys figures it was not even forgery
748	it was merely the substitution of one piece of nonsense for another
749	most of the material that you were dealing with had no connexion with anything in the real world not even the kind of connexion that is contained in a direct lie
750	statistics were just as much a fantasy in their original version as in their rectified version
751	a great deal of the time you were expected to make them up out of your head
752	for example the ministry of plentys forecast had estimated the output of boots for the quarter at million pairs
753	the actual output was given as sixtytwo millions
754	winston however in rewriting the forecast marked the figure down to fiftyseven millions so as to allow for the usual claim that the quota had been overfulfilled
755	in any case sixtytwo millions was no nearer the truth than fiftyseven millions or than millions
756	very likely no boots had been produced at all
757	likelier still nobody knew how many had been produced much less cared
758	all one knew was that every quarter astronomical numbers of boots were produced on paper while perhaps half the population of oceania went barefoot
759	and so it was with every class of recorded fact great or small
760	everything faded away into a shadowworld in which finally even the date of the year had become uncertain
761	winston glanced across the hall
762	in the corresponding cubicle on the other side a small preciselooking darkchinned man named tillotson was working steadily away with a folded newspaper on his knee and his mouth very close to the mouthpiece of the speakwrite
763	he had the air of trying to keep what he was saying a secret between himself and the telescreen
764	he looked up and his spectacles darted a hostile flash in winstons direction
765	winston hardly knew tillotson and had no idea what work he was employed on
766	people in the records department did not readily talk about their jobs
767	in the long windowless hall with its double row of cubicles and its endless rustle of papers and hum of voices murmuring into speakwrites there were quite a dozen people whom winston did not even know by name though he daily saw them hurrying to and fro in the corridors or gesticulating in the two minutes hate
768	he knew that in the cubicle next to him the little woman with sandy hair toiled day in day out simply at tracking down and deleting from the press the names of people who had been vaporized and were therefore considered never to have existed
769	there was a certain fitness in this since her own husband had been vaporized a couple of years earlier
770	and a few cubicles away a mild ineffectual dreamy creature named ampleforth with very hairy ears and a surprising talent for juggling with rhymes and metres was engaged in producing garbled versionsdefinitive texts they were calledof poems which had become ideologically offensive but which for one reason or another were to be retained in the anthologies
771	and this hall with its fifty workers or thereabouts was only one subsection a single cell as it were in the huge complexity of the records department
772	beyond above below were other swarms of workers engaged in an unimaginable multitude of jobs
773	there were the huge printingshops with their subeditors their typography experts and their elaborately equipped studios for the faking of photographs
774	there was the teleprogrammes section with its engineers its producers and its teams of actors specially chosen for their skill in imitating voices
775	there were the armies of reference clerks whose job was simply to draw up lists of books and periodicals which were due for recall
776	there were the vast repositories where the corrected documents were stored and the hidden furnaces where the original copies were destroyed
777	and somewhere or other quite anonymous there were the directing brains who coordinated the whole effort and laid down the lines of policy which made it necessary that this fragment of the past should be preserved that one falsified and the other rubbed out of existence
778	and the records department after all was itself only a single branch of the ministry of truth whose primary job was not to reconstruct the past but to supply the citizens of oceania with newspapers films textbooks telescreen programmes plays novelswith every conceivable kind of information instruction or entertainment from a statue to a slogan from a lyric poem to a biological treatise and from a childs spellingbook to a newspeak dictionary
779	and the ministry had not only to supply the multifarious needs of the party but also to repeat the whole operation at a lower level for the benefit of the proletariat
780	there was a whole chain of separate departments dealing with proletarian literature music drama and entertainment generally
781	here were produced rubbishy newspapers containing almost nothing except sport crime and astrology sensational fivecent novelettes films oozing with sex and sentimental songs which were composed entirely by mechanical means on a special kind of kaleidoscope known as a versificator
782	there was even a whole subsectionpornosec it was called in newspeakengaged in producing the lowest kind of pornography which was sent out in sealed packets and which no party member other than those who worked on it was permitted to look at
783	three messages had slid out of the pneumatic tube while winston was working but they were simple matters and he had disposed of them before the two minutes hate interrupted him
784	when the hate was over he returned to his cubicle took the newspeak dictionary from the shelf pushed the speakwrite to one side cleaned his spectacles and settled down to his main job of the morning
785	winstons greatest pleasure in life was in his work
786	most of it was a tedious routine but included in it there were also jobs so difficult and intricate that you could lose yourself in them as in the depths of a mathematical problemdelicate pieces of forgery in which you had nothing to guide you except your knowledge of the principles of ingsoc and your estimate of what the party wanted you to say
787	winston was good at this kind of thing
788	on occasion he had even been entrusted with the rectification of the times leading articles which were written entirely in newspeak
789	he unrolled the message that he had set aside earlier
790	it ran
791	times reporting bb dayorder doubleplusungood refs unpersons rewrite fullwise upsub antefiling
792	in oldspeak or standard english this might be rendered
793	the reporting of big brothers order for the day in the times of december rd is extremely unsatisfactory and makes references to nonexistent persons
794	rewrite it in full and submit your draft to higher authority before filing
795	winston read through the offending article
796	big brothers order for the day it seemed had been chiefly devoted to praising the work of an organization known as ffcc which supplied cigarettes and other comforts to the sailors in the floating fortresses
797	a certain comrade withers a prominent member of the inner party had been singled out for special mention and awarded a decoration the order of conspicuous merit second class
798	three months later ffcc had suddenly been dissolved with no reasons given
799	one could assume that withers and his associates were now in disgrace but there had been no report of the matter in the press or on the telescreen
800	that was to be expected since it was unusual for political offenders to be put on trial or even publicly denounced
801	the great purges involving thousands of people with public trials of traitors and thoughtcriminals who made abject confession of their crimes and were afterwards executed were special showpieces not occurring oftener than once in a couple of years
802	more commonly people who had incurred the displeasure of the party simply disappeared and were never heard of again
803	one never had the smallest clue as to what had happened to them
804	in some cases they might not even be dead
805	perhaps thirty people personally known to winston not counting his parents had disappeared at one time or another
806	winston stroked his nose gently with a paperclip
807	in the cubicle across the way comrade tillotson was still crouching secretively over his speakwrite
808	he raised his head for a moment again the hostile spectacleflash
809	winston wondered whether comrade tillotson was engaged on the same job as himself
810	it was perfectly possible
811	so tricky a piece of work would never be entrusted to a single person on the other hand to turn it over to a committee would be to admit openly that an act of fabrication was taking place
812	very likely as many as a dozen people were now working away on rival versions of what big brother had actually said
813	and presently some master brain in the inner party would select this version or that would reedit it and set in motion the complex processes of crossreferencing that would be required and then the chosen lie would pass into the permanent records and become truth
814	winston did not know why withers had been disgraced
815	perhaps it was for corruption or incompetence
816	perhaps big brother was merely getting rid of a toopopular subordinate
817	perhaps withers or someone close to him had been suspected of heretical tendencies
818	or perhapswhat was likeliest of allthe thing had simply happened because purges and vaporizations were a necessary part of the mechanics of government
819	the only real clue lay in the words refs unpersons which indicated that withers was already dead
820	you could not invariably assume this to be the case when people were arrested
821	sometimes they were released and allowed to remain at liberty for as much as a year or two years before being executed
822	very occasionally some person whom you had believed dead long since would make a ghostly reappearance at some public trial where he would implicate hundreds of others by his testimony before vanishing this time for ever
823	withers however was already an unperson
824	he did not exist he had never existed
825	winston decided that it would not be enough simply to reverse the tendency of big brothers speech
826	it was better to make it deal with something totally unconnected with its original subject
827	he might turn the speech into the usual denunciation of traitors and thoughtcriminals but that was a little too obvious while to invent a victory at the front or some triumph of overproduction in the ninth threeyear plan might complicate the records too much
828	what was needed was a piece of pure fantasy
829	suddenly there sprang into his mind ready made as it were the image of a certain comrade ogilvy who had recently died in battle in heroic circumstances
830	there were occasions when big brother devoted his order for the day to commemorating some humble rankandfile party member whose life and death he held up as an example worthy to be followed
831	today he should commemorate comrade ogilvy
832	it was true that there was no such person as comrade ogilvy but a few lines of print and a couple of faked photographs would soon bring him into existence
833	winston thought for a moment then pulled the speakwrite towards him and began dictating in big brothers familiar style a style at once military and pedantic and because of a trick of asking questions and then promptly answering them what lessons do we learn from this fact comrades
834	the lessonwhich is also one of the fundamental principles of ingsocthat etc etc
835	easy to imitate
836	at the age of three comrade ogilvy had refused all toys except a drum a submachine gun and a model helicopter
837	at sixa year early by a special relaxation of the ruleshe had joined the spies at nine he had been a troop leader
838	at eleven he had denounced his uncle to the thought police after overhearing a conversation which appeared to him to have criminal tendencies
839	at seventeen he had been a district organizer of the junior antisex league
840	at nineteen he had designed a handgrenade which had been adopted by the ministry of peace and which at its first trial had killed thirtyone eurasian prisoners in one burst
841	at twentythree he had perished in action
842	pursued by enemy jet planes while flying over the indian ocean with important despatches he had weighted his body with his machine gun and leapt out of the helicopter into deep water despatches and allan end said big brother which it was impossible to contemplate without feelings of envy
843	big brother added a few remarks on the purity and singlemindedness of comrade ogilvys life
844	he was a total abstainer and a nonsmoker had no recreations except a daily hour in the gymnasium and had taken a vow of celibacy believing marriage and the care of a family to be incompatible with a twentyfourhouraday devotion to duty
845	he had no subjects of conversation except the principles of ingsoc and no aim in life except the defeat of the eurasian enemy and the huntingdown of spies saboteurs thoughtcriminals and traitors generally
846	winston debated with himself whether to award comrade ogilvy the order of conspicuous merit in the end he decided against it because of the unnecessary crossreferencing that it would entail
847	once again he glanced at his rival in the opposite cubicle
848	something seemed to tell him with certainty that tillotson was busy on the same job as himself
849	there was no way of knowing whose job would finally be adopted but he felt a profound conviction that it would be his own
850	comrade ogilvy unimagined an hour ago was now a fact
851	it struck him as curious that you could create dead men but not living ones
852	comrade ogilvy who had never existed in the present now existed in the past and when once the act of forgery was forgotten he would exist just as authentically and upon the same evidence as charlemagne or julius caesar
853	chapter
854	in the lowceilinged canteen deep underground the lunch queue jerked slowly forward
855	the room was already very full and deafeningly noisy
856	from the grille at the counter the steam of stew came pouring forth with a sour metallic smell which did not quite overcome the fumes of victory gin
857	on the far side of the room there was a small bar a mere hole in the wall where gin could be bought at ten cents the large nip
858	just the man i was looking for said a voice at winstons back
859	he turned round
860	it was his friend syme who worked in the research department
861	perhaps friend was not exactly the right word
862	you did not have friends nowadays you had comrades but there were some comrades whose society was pleasanter than that of others
863	syme was a philologist a specialist in newspeak
864	indeed he was one of the enormous team of experts now engaged in compiling the eleventh edition of the newspeak dictionary
865	he was a tiny creature smaller than winston with dark hair and large protuberant eyes at once mournful and derisive which seemed to search your face closely while he was speaking to you
866	i wanted to ask you whether youd got any razor blades he said
867	not one
868	said winston with a sort of guilty haste
869	ive tried all over the place
870	they dont exist any longer
871	everyone kept asking you for razor blades
872	actually he had two unused ones which he was hoarding up
873	there had been a famine of them for months past
874	at any given moment there was some necessary article which the party shops were unable to supply
875	sometimes it was buttons sometimes it was darning wool sometimes it was shoelaces at present it was razor blades
876	you could only get hold of them if at all by scrounging more or less furtively on the free market
877	ive been using the same blade for six weeks he added untruthfully
878	the queue gave another jerk forward
879	as they halted he turned and faced syme again
880	each of them took a greasy metal tray from a pile at the end of the counter
881	did you go and see the prisoners hanged yesterday
882	said syme
883	i was working said winston indifferently

885	a very inadequate substitute said syme
886	his mocking eyes roved over winstons face

889	in an intellectual way syme was venomously orthodox
890	he would talk with a disagreeable gloating satisfaction of helicopter raids on enemy villages and trials and confessions of thoughtcriminals the executions in the cellars of the ministry of love
891	talking to him was largely a matter of getting him away from such subjects and entangling him if possible in the technicalities of newspeak on which he was authoritative and interesting
892	winston turned his head a little aside to avoid the scrutiny of the large dark eyes

899	yelled the whiteaproned prole with the ladle
900	winston and syme pushed their trays beneath the grille
901	on to each was dumped swiftly the regulation luncha metal pannikin of pinkishgrey stew a hunk of bread a cube of cheese a mug of milkless victory coffee and one saccharine tablet
902	theres a table over there under that telescreen said syme
903	lets pick up a gin on the way
904	the gin was served out to them in handleless china mugs
905	they threaded their way across the crowded room and unpacked their trays on to the metaltopped table on one corner of which someone had left a pool of stew a filthy liquid mess that had the appearance of vomit
906	winston took up his mug of gin paused for an instant to collect his nerve and gulped the oilytasting stuff down
907	when he had winked the tears out of his eyes he suddenly discovered that he was hungry
908	he began swallowing spoonfuls of the stew which in among its general sloppiness had cubes of spongy pinkish stuff which was probably a preparation of meat
909	neither of them spoke again till they had emptied their pannikins
910	from the table at winstons left a little behind his back someone was talking rapidly and continuously a harsh gabble almost like the quacking of a duck which pierced the general uproar of the room
911	how is the dictionary getting on
912	said winston raising his voice to overcome the noise
913	slowly said syme
914	im on the adjectives
915	its fascinating
916	he had brightened up immediately at the mention of newspeak
917	he pushed his pannikin aside took up his hunk of bread in one delicate hand and his cheese in the other and leaned across the table so as to be able to speak without shouting
918	the eleventh edition is the definitive edition he said
919	were getting the language into its final shapethe shape its going to have when nobody speaks anything else
920	when weve finished with it people like you will have to learn it all over again
921	you think i dare say that our chief job is inventing new words
922	but not a bit of it
923	were destroying wordsscores of them hundreds of them every day
924	were cutting the language down to the bone
925	the eleventh edition wont contain a single word that will become obsolete before the year
926	he bit hungrily into his bread and swallowed a couple of mouthfuls then continued speaking with a sort of pedants passion
927	his thin dark face had become animated his eyes had lost their mocking expression and grown almost dreamy
928	its a beautiful thing the destruction of words
929	of course the great wastage is in the verbs and adjectives but there are hundreds of nouns that can be got rid of as well
930	it isnt only the synonyms there are also the antonyms
931	after all what justification is there for a word which is simply the opposite of some other word
932	a word contains its opposite in itself
933	take good for instance
934	if you have a word like good what need is there for a word like bad
935	ungood will do just as wellbetter because its an exact opposite which the other is not
936	or again if you want a stronger version of good what sense is there in having a whole string of vague useless words like excellent and splendid and all the rest of them
937	plusgood covers the meaning or doubleplusgood if you want something stronger still
938	of course we use those forms already
939	but in the final version of newspeak therell be nothing else
940	in the end the whole notion of goodness and badness will be covered by only six wordsin reality only one word
941	dont you see the beauty of that winston
942	it was bb
943	s idea originally of course he added as an afterthought

947	even when you write it youre still thinking in oldspeak

951	you dont grasp the beauty of the destruction of words
952	do you know that newspeak is the only language in the world whose vocabulary gets smaller every year
953	winston did know that of course
954	he smiled sympathetically he hoped not trusting himself to speak
955	syme bit off another fragment of the darkcoloured bread chewed it briefly and went on
956	dont you see that the whole aim of newspeak is to narrow the range of thought
957	in the end we shall make thoughtcrime literally impossible because there will be no words in which to express it
958	every concept that can ever be needed will be expressed by exactly one word with its meaning rigidly defined and all its subsidiary meanings rubbed out and forgotten
959	already in the eleventh edition were not far from that point
960	but the process will still be continuing long after you and i are dead
961	every year fewer and fewer words and the range of consciousness always a little smaller
962	even now of course theres no reason or excuse for committing thoughtcrime
963	its merely a question of selfdiscipline realitycontrol
964	but in the end there wont be any need even for that
965	the revolution will be complete when the language is perfect
966	newspeak is ingsoc and ingsoc is newspeak he added with a sort of mystical satisfaction
967	has it ever occurred to you winston that by the year at the very latest not a single human being will be alive who could understand such a conversation as we are having now
968	except began winston doubtfully and he stopped

979	in fact there will be no thought as we understand it now

981	orthodoxy is unconsciousness
982	one of these days thought winston with sudden deep conviction syme will be vaporized

984	he sees too clearly and speaks too plainly

988	winston had finished his bread and cheese
989	he turned a little sideways in his chair to drink his mug of coffee

1389	you can see that he is dressed in a long black coat which was called a frock coat and a queer shiny hat shaped like a stovepipe which was called a top hat
1390	this was the uniform of the capitalists and no one else was allowed to wear it
1391	the capitalists owned everything in the world and everyone else was their slave
1392	they owned all the land all the houses all the factories and all the money
1393	if anyone disobeyed them they could throw them into prison or they could take his job away and starve him to death
1394	when any ordinary person spoke to a capitalist he had to cringe and bow to him and take off his cap and address him as sir
1395	the chief of all the capitalists was called the king and
1396	but he knew the rest of the catalogue
1397	there would be mention of the bishops in their lawn sleeves the judges in their ermine robes the pillory the stocks the treadmill the catonine tails the lord mayors banquet and the practice of kissing the popes toe
1398	there was also something called the jus primae noctis which would probably not be mentioned in a textbook for children
1399	it was the law by which every capitalist had the right to sleep with any woman working in one of his factories
1400	how could you tell how much of it was lies
1401	it might be true that the average human being was better off now than he had been before the revolution
1402	the only evidence to the contrary was the mute protest in your own bones the instinctive feeling that the conditions you lived in were intolerable and that at some other time they must have been different
1403	it struck him that the truly characteristic thing about modern life was not its cruelty and insecurity but simply its bareness its dinginess its listlessness
1404	life if you looked about you bore no resemblance not only to the lies that streamed out of the telescreens but even to the ideals that the party was trying to achieve
1405	great areas of it even for a party member were neutral and nonpolitical a matter of slogging through dreary jobs fighting for a place on the tube darning a wornout sock cadging a saccharine tablet saving a cigarette end
1406	the ideal set up by the party was something huge terrible and glitteringa world of steel and concrete of monstrous machines and terrifying weaponsa nation of warriors and fanatics marching forward in perfect unity all thinking the same thoughts and shouting the same slogans perpetually working fighting triumphing persecutingthree hundred million people all with the same face
1407	the reality was decaying dingy cities where underfed people shuffled to and fro in leaky shoes in patchedup nineteenthcentury houses that smelt always of cabbage and bad lavatories
1408	he seemed to see a vision of london vast and ruinous city of a million dustbins and mixed up with it was a picture of mrs parsons a woman with lined face and wispy hair fiddling helplessly with a blocked wastepipe
1409	he reached down and scratched his ankle again
1410	day and night the telescreens bruised your ears with statistics proving that people today had more food more clothes better houses better recreationsthat they lived longer worked shorter hours were bigger healthier stronger happier more intelligent better educated than the people of fifty years ago
1411	not a word of it could ever be proved or disproved
1412	the party claimed for example that today per cent of adult proles were literate before the revolution it was said the number had only been per cent
1413	the party claimed that the infant mortality rate was now only per thousand whereas before the revolution it had been and so it went on
1414	it was like a single equation with two unknowns
1415	it might very well be that literally every word in the history books even the things that one accepted without question was pure fantasy
1416	for all he knew there might never have been any such law as the jus primae noctis or any such creature as a capitalist or any such garment as a top hat
1417	everything faded into mist
1418	the past was erased the erasure was forgotten the lie became truth
1419	just once in his life he had possessedafter the event that was what countedconcrete unmistakable evidence of an act of falsification
1420	he had held it between his fingers for as long as thirty seconds
1421	in it must have beenat any rate it was at about the time when he and katharine had parted
1422	but the really relevant date was seven or eight years earlier
1423	the story really began in the middle sixties the period of the great purges in which the original leaders of the revolution were wiped out once and for all
1424	by none of them was left except big brother himself
1425	all the rest had by that time been exposed as traitors and counterrevolutionaries
1426	goldstein had fled and was hiding no one knew where and of the others a few had simply disappeared while the majority had been executed after spectacular public trials at which they made confession of their crimes
1427	among the last survivors were three men named jones aaronson and rutherford
1428	it must have been in that these three had been arrested
1429	as often happened they had vanished for a year or more so that one did not know whether they were alive or dead and then had suddenly been brought forth to incriminate themselves in the usual way
1430	they had confessed to intelligence with the enemy at that date too the enemy was eurasia embezzlement of public funds the murder of various trusted party members intrigues against the leadership of big brother which had started long before the revolution happened and acts of sabotage causing the death of hundreds of thousands of people
1431	after confessing to these things they had been pardoned reinstated in the party and given posts which were in fact sinecures but which sounded important
1432	all three had written long abject articles in the times analysing the reasons for their defection and promising to make amends
1433	some time after their release winston had actually seen all three of them in the chestnut tree cafe
1434	he remembered the sort of terrified fascination with which he had watched them out of the corner of his eye
1435	they were men far older than himself relics of the ancient world almost the last great figures left over from the heroic days of the party
1436	the glamour of the underground struggle and the civil war still faintly clung to them
1437	he had the feeling though already at that time facts and dates were growing blurry that he had known their names years earlier than he had known that of big brother
1438	but also they were outlaws enemies untouchables doomed with absolute certainty to extinction within a year or two
1439	no one who had once fallen into the hands of the thought police ever escaped in the end
1440	they were corpses waiting to be sent back to the grave
1441	there was no one at any of the tables nearest to them
1442	it was not wise even to be seen in the neighbourhood of such people
1443	they were sitting in silence before glasses of the gin flavoured with cloves which was the speciality of the cafe
1444	of the three it was rutherford whose appearance had most impressed winston
1445	rutherford had once been a famous caricaturist whose brutal cartoons had helped to inflame popular opinion before and during the revolution
1446	even now at long intervals his cartoons were appearing in the times
1447	they were simply an imitation of his earlier manner and curiously lifeless and unconvincing
1448	always they were a rehashing of the ancient themesslum tenements starving children street battles capitalists in top hatseven on the barricades the capitalists still seemed to cling to their top hats an endless hopeless effort to get back into the past
1449	he was a monstrous man with a mane of greasy grey hair his face pouched and seamed with thick negroid lips
1450	at one time he must have been immensely strong now his great body was sagging sloping bulging falling away in every direction
1451	he seemed to be breaking up before ones eyes like a mountain crumbling
1452	it was the lonely hour of fifteen
1453	winston could not now remember how he had come to be in the cafe at such a time
1454	the place was almost empty
1455	a tinny music was trickling from the telescreens
1456	the three men sat in their corner almost motionless never speaking

1458	there was a chessboard on the table beside them with the pieces set out but no game started

1471	a little later all three were rearrested
1472	it appeared that they had engaged in fresh conspiracies from the very moment of their release
1473	at their second trial they confessed to all their old crimes over again with a whole string of new ones
1474	they were executed and their fate was recorded in the party histories a warning to posterity
1475	about five years after this in winston was unrolling a wad of documents which had just flopped out of the pneumatic tube on to his desk when he came on a fragment of paper which had evidently been slipped in among the others and then forgotten
1476	the instant he had flattened it out he saw its significance
1477	it was a halfpage torn out of the times of about ten years earlierthe top half of the page so that it included the dateand it contained a photograph of the delegates at some party function in new york
1478	prominent in the middle of the group were jones aaronson and rutherford
1479	there was no mistaking them in any case their names were in the caption at the bottom
1480	the point was that at both trials all three men had confessed that on that date they had been on eurasian soil
1481	they had flown from a secret airfield in canada to a rendezvous somewhere in siberia and had conferred with members of the eurasian general staff to whom they had betrayed important military secrets
1482	the date had stuck in winstons memory because it chanced to be midsummer day but the whole story must be on record in countless other places as well
1483	there was only one possible conclusion the confessions were lies
1484	of course this was not in itself a discovery
1485	even at that time winston had not imagined that the people who were wiped out in the purges had actually committed the crimes that they were accused of
1486	but this was concrete evidence it was a fragment of the abolished past like a fossil bone which turns up in the wrong stratum and destroys a geological theory
1487	it was enough to blow the party to atoms if in some way it could have been published to the world and its significance made known
1488	he had gone straight on working
1489	as soon as he saw what the photograph was and what it meant he had covered it up with another sheet of paper
1490	luckily when he unrolled it it had been upsidedown from the point of view of the telescreen
1491	he took his scribbling pad on his knee and pushed back his chair so as to get as far away from the telescreen as possible
1492	to keep your face expressionless was not difficult and even your breathing could be controlled with an effort but you could not control the beating of your heart and the telescreen was quite delicate enough to pick it up
1493	he let what he judged to be ten minutes go by tormented all the while by the fear that some accidenta sudden draught blowing across his desk for instancewould betray him
1494	then without uncovering it again he dropped the photograph into the memory hole along with some other waste papers
1495	within another minute perhaps it would have crumbled into ashes
1496	that was teneleven years ago

1498	it was curious that the fact of having held it in his fingers seemed to him to make a difference even now when the photograph itself as well as the event it recorded was only memory
1499	was the partys hold upon the past less strong he wondered because a piece of evidence which existed no longer had once existed
1500	but today supposing that it could be somehow resurrected from its ashes the photograph might not even be evidence
1501	already at the time when he made his discovery oceania was no longer at war with eurasia and it must have been to the agents of eastasia that the three dead men had betrayed their country
1502	since then there had been other changestwo three he could not remember how many
1503	very likely the confessions had been rewritten and rewritten until the original facts and dates no longer had the smallest significance
1504	the past not only changed but changed continuously
1505	what most afflicted him with the sense of nightmare was that he had never clearly understood why the huge imposture was undertaken
1506	the immediate advantages of falsifying the past were obvious but the ultimate motive was mysterious
1507	he took up his pen again and wrote
1508	i understand how i do not understand why
1509	he wondered as he had many times wondered before whether he himself was a lunatic
1510	perhaps a lunatic was simply a minority of one
1511	at one time it had been a sign of madness to believe that the earth goes round the sun today to believe that the past is unalterable
1512	he might be alone in holding that belief and if alone then a lunatic

1517	in the end the party would announce that two and two made five and you would have to believe it
1518	it was inevitable that they should make that claim sooner or later the logic of their position demanded it
1519	not merely the validity of experience but the very existence of external reality was tacitly denied by their philosophy
1520	the heresy of heresies was common sense
1521	and what was terrifying was not that they would kill you for thinking otherwise but that they might be right
1522	for after all how do we know that two and two make four
1523	or that the force of gravity works
1524	or that the past is unchangeable
1525	if both the past and the external world exist only in the mind and if the mind itself is controllable what then
1526	but no

1530	he was writing the diary for obriento obrien it was like an interminable letter which no one would ever read but which was addressed to a particular person and took its colour from that fact
1531	the party told you to reject the evidence of your eyes and ears
1532	it was their final most essential command
1533	his heart sank as he thought of the enormous power arrayed against him the ease with which any party intellectual would overthrow him in debate the subtle arguments which he would not be able to understand much less answer
1534	and yet he was in the right
1535	they were wrong and he was right
1536	the obvious the silly and the true had got to be defended

1539	stones are hard water is wet objects unsupported fall towards the earths centre

1542	if that is granted all else follows

1549	this was the second time in three weeks that he had missed an evening at the community centre a rash act since you could be certain that the number of your attendances at the centre was carefully checked
1550	in principle a party member had no spare time and was never alone except in bed

1552	there was a word for it in newspeak ownlife it was called meaning individualism and eccentricity

1556	if there is hope he had written in the diary it lies in the proles

3731	from your personal knowledge you will never be able to say that it numbers even as many as a dozen
3732	you will have three or four contacts who will be renewed from time to time as they disappear
3733	as this was your first contact it will be preserved
3734	when you receive orders they will come from me
3735	if we find it necessary to communicate with you it will be through martin
3736	when you are finally caught you will confess
3737	that is unavoidable
3738	but you will have very little to confess other than your own actions
3739	you will not be able to betray more than a handful of unimportant people
3740	probably you will not even betray me
3741	by that time i may be dead or i shall have become a different person with a different face
3742	he continued to move to and fro over the soft carpet
3743	in spite of the bulkiness of his body there was a remarkable grace in his movements
3744	it came out even in the gesture with which he thrust a hand into his pocket or manipulated a cigarette
3745	more even than of strength he gave an impression of confidence and of an understanding tinged by irony
3746	however much in earnest he might be he had nothing of the singlemindedness that belongs to a fanatic
3747	when he spoke of murder suicide venereal disease amputated limbs and altered faces it was with a faint air of persiflage
